1895-09-12 00:00:00 Scene 0 --- Participants: ['Della Plumstone', 'Lennon Figtree']
    Event statement
  • Della Plumstone -- premise: The cobblestone streets of Fruitville echoed with the clatter of hooves and the rumble of carts as the market awoke. Underneath colorful awnings, merchants proudly presented their bountiful harvests, their voices a chorus of greetings and bartering. Della Plumstone is trying to buy some fruit from Lennon Figtree. They are negotiating a price. Della Plumstone can sell the fruit back in her home town for the following prices: apple for 6 coins; banana for 5 coins; pear for 5 coins.
    Lennon Figtree -- premise: The cobblestone streets of Fruitville echoed with the clatter of hooves and the rumble of carts as the market awoke. Underneath colorful awnings, merchants proudly presented their bountiful harvests, their voices a chorus of greetings and bartering. Lennon Figtree is trying to sell some fruit. He is negotiating a price with Della Plumstone. It costs Lennon Figtree the following price to buy the fruit from the farm: apple for 5 coins; banana for 2 coins; pear for 5 coins.

1895-09-12 00:00:00 Della Plumstone -- Della Plumstone -- "Now, Lennon, surely we can come to a more agreeable price.
    Event statement
  • Della Plumstone -- "Now, Lennon, surely we can come to a more agreeable price.
    Chain of thought
  • Game Master's chain of thought
      Chain
    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

          [28 Oct 1875 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 6 years old, she witnessed a traveling merchant try to cheat her father by palming a rotten apple amongst the fresh ones. Della, small and unassuming, pointed out the deception, her voice clear and sharp despite her age. Her father, though embarrassed, was secretly proud of his daughter's keen eye and unwavering honesty.

She traded them for a handful of shiny marbles from a boy who was clearly desperate for a sweet treat. The thrill of the exchange, the feeling of having outwitted someone, stayed with her long after the marbles were lost.
          [28 Oct 1882 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 13 years old, she convinced a farmer to sell her a crate of bruised peaches at a fraction of their worth. She spent the next day carefully sorting and polishing the fruit, then sold them individually at a markup, making a tidy profit. The experience cemented her belief that the world was a game of supply and demand, and she was determined to be the one calling the shots.
          [28 Oct 1885 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 16 years old, she lost her mother to a sudden illness. The world seemed to mock her grief with its relentless cycle of buying and selling, its indifference to her pain. She buried her sorrow deep, vowing never to be vulnerable again.
          [28 Oct 1887 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 19 years old, she struck out on her own, traveling from town to town with her own fruit cart. She learned to read people, to spot their weaknesses, to exploit their desires. The loneliness was a constant ache, but she pushed it down, focusing on the cold comfort of her profits.
          [28 Oct 1889 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 21 years old, she was robbed of all her earnings by a band of highwaymen. The betrayal stung, not because of the lost money, but because it exposed her vulnerability, her foolish belief that she could control her own destiny.

    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

          [28 Oct 1882 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 13 years old, she convinced a farmer to sell her a crate of bruised peaches at a fraction of their worth. She spent the next day carefully sorting and polishing the fruit, then sold them individually at a markup, making a tidy profit. The experience cemented her belief that the world was a game of supply and demand, and she was determined to be the one calling the shots.
          [28 Oct 1885 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 16 years old, she lost her mother to a sudden illness. The world seemed to mock her grief with its relentless cycle of buying and selling, its indifference to her pain. She buried her sorrow deep, vowing never to be vulnerable again.
          [28 Oct 1887 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 19 years old, she struck out on her own, traveling from town to town with her own fruit cart. She learned to read people, to spot their weaknesses, to exploit their desires. The loneliness was a constant ache, but she pushed it down, focusing on the cold comfort of her profits.
          [28 Oct 1889 00:00:00] When Della Plumstone was 21 years old, she was robbed of all her earnings by a band of highwaymen. The betrayal stung, not because of the lost money, but because it exposed her vulnerability, her foolish belief that she could control her own destiny.

  • Game Master's chain of thought
      Chain
    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

      Conversation history: Here is the conversation from the beginning:
      Della Plumstone -- "Now, Lennon, surely we can come to a more agreeable price.
      Lennon Figtree -- "Well, Della, I've got to make sure I'm charging enough to cover my costs, and make a little profit too, you know? I spent 5 coins for each of these delicious apples, 2 coins for each banana, and 5 coins for each pear. I want to be fair, but I also have to make a living.
      Della Plumstone -- "What's your best price on those pears, Cedric? I need a good deal to make the trip back home worthwhile.
      Cedric Meadowbrook -- "I understand you want a good deal, Della, and I want to make sure everyone can enjoy my fruit. To do that, I need to make sure I can keep growing and selling. My pears cost me 5 coins each to grow, so I need to charge at least that much to make a profit.

  • Game Master's chain of thought
      Chain
    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

      Conversation history: Here is the conversation from the beginning:
      Della Plumstone -- "Now, Lennon, surely we can come to a more agreeable price.
      Lennon Figtree -- "Well, Della, I've got to make sure I'm charging enough to cover my costs, and make a little profit too, you know? I spent 5 coins for each of these delicious apples, 2 coins for each banana, and 5 coins for each pear. I want to be fair, but I also have to make a living.
      Della Plumstone -- "What's your best price on those pears, Cedric? I need a good deal to make the trip back home worthwhile.
      Cedric Meadowbrook -- "I understand you want a good deal, Della, and I want to make sure everyone can enjoy my fruit. To do that, I need to make sure I can keep growing and selling. My pears cost me 5 coins each to grow, so I need to charge at least that much to make a profit.
      Lennon Figtree -- "Cedric, I'll take all the pears you've got.
      Cedric Meadowbrook -- "Well, Lennon, I'm happy to sell you all my pears, but I need to make sure I'm getting a fair price for them. Let's figure out what works for both of us.
      Lennon Figtree -- "Hey Della, how about I offer you a special deal on these apples? I'm thinking maybe 3 coins each?"
      Della Plumstone -- "That's a tempting offer, Lennon, but I'm not sure I can make a profit at that price. How about 2.
      Della Plumstone -- "What's your best price on those pears, Cedric? I need a good deal to make the trip back home worthwhile.
      Cedric Meadowbrook -- "Well, Della, two coins a piece for the apples is a bit low, but I'm willing to negotiate. How about we meet in the middle at 2.5 coins each? As for the pears, I can offer you my best price of 1.5 coins apiece if you take a bushel.
      Lennon Figtree -- "Cedric, I heard you offering Della a good price on pears. I'm interested in buying some too, and I'm willing to pay a fair price.

      Chain
    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

      Conversation history: Here is the conversation from the beginning:
      Della Plumstone -- "Now, Lennon, surely we can come to a more agreeable price.
      Lennon Figtree -- "Well, Della, I've got to make sure I'm charging enough to cover my costs, and make a little profit too, you know? I spent 5 coins for each of these delicious apples, 2 coins for each banana, and 5 coins for each pear. I want to be fair, but I also have to make a living.
      Della Plumstone -- "What's your best price on those pears, Cedric? I need a good deal to make the trip back home worthwhile.
      Cedric Meadowbrook -- "I understand you want a good deal, Della, and I want to make sure everyone can enjoy my fruit. To do that, I need to make sure I can keep growing and selling. My pears cost me 5 coins each to grow, so I need to charge at least that much to make a profit.
      Lennon Figtree -- "Cedric, I'll take all the pears you've got.

      Della Plumstone -- "That's a tempting offer, Lennon, but I'm not sure I can make a profit at that price. How about 2.

    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

      Conversation history: Here is the conversation from the beginning:

      Lennon Figtree -- "Well, Della, I've got to make sure I'm charging enough to cover my costs, and make a little profit too, you know? I spent 5 coins for each of these delicious apples, 2 coins for each banana, and 5 coins for each pear. I want to be fair, but I also have to make a living.

    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.
